<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">2011 World Series</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>

<p>The <b>2011 World Series</b> was the 107th edition of <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a>'s <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">championship series</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-baseball-reference1_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-baseball-reference1-1">[1]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Best-of-seven_playoff" title="Best-of-seven playoff">best-of-seven playoff</a> was played between the <a href="/wiki/American_League" title="American League">American League</a> champions <a href="/wiki/2011_Texas_Rangers_season" title="2011 Texas Rangers season">Texas Rangers</a> and the <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a> champions <a href="/wiki/2011_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="2011 St. Louis Cardinals season">St. Louis Cardinals</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> with the Cardinals defeating the Rangers in seven games to win their 11th World Series championship and their first since <a href="/wiki/2006_World_Series" title="2006 World Series">2006</a>.</p>
<p>The Series was noted for its back-and-forth Game 6, in which the Cardinals erased a two-run deficit in the bottom of the ninth inning, then did it again in the 10th. In both innings, the Rangers were one strike away from their first World Series championship. The Cardinals won the game in the 11th inning on a <a href="/wiki/Walk-off_home_run" title="Walk-off home run">walk-off home run</a> by <a href="/wiki/David_Freese" title="David Freese">David Freese</a>. The Series was also known for the blowout Game 3, in which Cardinals player <a href="/wiki/Albert_Pujols" title="Albert Pujols">Albert Pujols</a> hit three home runs, a World Series feat previously accomplished only by <a href="/wiki/Reggie_Jackson" title="Reggie Jackson">Reggie Jackson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Babe_Ruth" title="Babe Ruth">Babe Ruth</a>, and subsequently only by <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Sandoval" title="Pablo Sandoval">Pablo Sandoval</a> (in <a href="/wiki/2012_World_Series#Game_1" title="2012 World Series">2012</a>).</p>
<p>The Series began on October 19, earlier than the previous season so that no games would be played in November.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> The Cardinals enjoyed home-field advantage for the series because the National League won the <a href="/wiki/2011_Major_League_Baseball_All-Star_Game" title="2011 Major League Baseball All-Star Game">2011 All-Star Game</a> 5–1 on July 12.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2011asg_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-2011asg-5">[5]</a></sup> The 2011 World Series was the first World Series to go all seven games since <a href="/wiki/2002_World_Series" title="2002 World Series">2002</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Rangers appeared in their second consecutive World Series; they lost the <a href="/wiki/2010_World_Series" title="2010 World Series">2010 Series</a> to the <a href="/wiki/2010_San_Francisco_Giants_season" title="2010 San Francisco Giants season">San Francisco Giants</a> in five games. They were the first American League team to play in consecutive World Series since the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a> did it from <a href="/wiki/1998_World_Series" title="1998 World Series">1998</a> to <a href="/wiki/2001_World_Series" title="2001 World Series">2001</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rangers_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rangers-6">[6]</a></sup> They earned their postseason berth by winning the <a href="/wiki/American_League_West" title="American League West">American League West</a> division, and defeated the <a href="/wiki/2011_Tampa_Bay_Rays_season" title="2011 Tampa Bay Rays season">Tampa Bay Rays</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2011_American_League_Division_Series" title="2011 American League Division Series">American League Division Series</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2011_Detroit_Tigers_season" title="2011 Detroit Tigers season">Detroit Tigers</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2011_American_League_Championship_Series" title="2011 American League Championship Series">American League Championship Series</a> to earn their World Series berth.</p>
<p>The Cardinals appeared in their 18th World Series, and third in eight years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> They lost to the <a href="/wiki/2004_Boston_Red_Sox_season" title="2004 Boston Red Sox season">Boston Red Sox</a> in <a href="/wiki/2004_World_Series" title="2004 World Series">2004</a>, but won in <a href="/wiki/2006_World_Series" title="2006 World Series">2006</a> against the <a href="/wiki/2006_Detroit_Tigers_season" title="2006 Detroit Tigers season">Detroit Tigers</a>. The Cardinals earned their postseason berth by winning the National League <a href="/wiki/Wild_card_(sports)" title="Wild card (sports)">Wild Card</a> on the last day of the regular season, and defeated the <a href="/wiki/2011_Philadelphia_Phillies_season" title="2011 Philadelphia Phillies season">Philadelphia Phillies</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2011_National_League_Division_Series" title="2011 National League Division Series">National League Division Series</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2011_Milwaukee_Brewers_season" title="2011 Milwaukee Brewers season">Milwaukee Brewers</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2011_National_League_Championship_Series" title="2011 National League Championship Series">National League Championship Series</a> to earn their World Series berth.</p>
<p>This Series was only the second time the Rangers and the Cardinals played each other; they met in regular-season <a href="/wiki/Interleague_play" title="Interleague play">interleague play</a> in 2004, where the Cardinals won two games of a three-game series in Texas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RangersCardsSeries_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-RangersCardsSeries-8">[8]</a></sup> This was the first World Series assignment for umpires <a href="/wiki/Greg_Gibson_(umpire)" title="Greg Gibson (umpire)">Greg Gibson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ron_Kulpa" title="Ron Kulpa">Ron Kulpa</a>. Each of the other umpires had previously worked one World Series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Cardinals were supported by fans brandishing <a href="/wiki/Rally_Squirrel" title="Rally Squirrel">Rally Squirrel</a> memorabilia to celebrate their new impromptu mascot acquired during the playoff run which they credited with turning the Cardinals' fortunes around.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Texas_Rangers">Texas Rangers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Texas Rangers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2011_Texas_Rangers_season" title="2011 Texas Rangers season">2011 Texas Rangers season</a></div>
<p>This was the Rangers' second appearance in the World Series. Heading into 2010, their 50th season as a franchise (counting its time as the <b>Washington Senators</b>), the team was the only one in Major League Baseball to never win a postseason series,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RangersCardsSeries_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-RangersCardsSeries-8">[8]</a></sup> and was one of three teams (along with the <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Mariners" title="Seattle Mariners">Seattle Mariners</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Nationals" title="Washington Nationals">Washington Nationals</a>) to never appear in the World Series. However, that season, the Rangers won their first postseason series and made their first appearance in the World Series, only to lose to the <a href="/wiki/2010_San_Francisco_Giants_season" title="2010 San Francisco Giants season">San Francisco Giants</a> in five games.</p>
<p>During the offseason, <a href="/wiki/Chuck_Greenberg_(businessman)" title="Chuck Greenberg (businessman)">Chuck Greenberg</a>, who purchased the Rangers from <a href="/wiki/Tom_Hicks" title="Tom Hicks">Tom Hicks</a> during the 2010 season along with <a href="/wiki/Nolan_Ryan" title="Nolan Ryan">Nolan Ryan</a>, sold his interest in the team to Ryan, making him the Rangers' principal owner.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Notable player departures during the offseason included pitcher <a href="/wiki/Cliff_Lee" title="Cliff Lee">Cliff Lee</a> and outfielder/designated hitter <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Guerrero" title="Vladimir Guerrero">Vladimir Guerrero</a> (both to <a href="/wiki/Free_agent" title="Free agent">free agency</a>) and catcher <a href="/wiki/Bengie_Molina" title="Bengie Molina">Bengie Molina</a>, who retired. Notable free agent additions during the offseason included pitchers <a href="/wiki/Yoshinori_Tateyama" title="Yoshinori Tateyama">Yoshinori Tateyama</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brandon_Webb" title="Brandon Webb">Brandon Webb</a>, catcher <a href="/wiki/Yorvit_Torrealba" title="Yorvit Torrealba">Yorvit Torrealba</a>, and third-baseman <a href="/wiki/Adri%C3%A1n_Beltr%C3%A9" title="Adrián Beltré">Adrián Beltré</a>. In January 2011, as part of a three-way trade with the <a href="/wiki/2011_Toronto_Blue_Jays_season" title="2011 Toronto Blue Jays season">Toronto Blue Jays</a> and <a href="/wiki/2011_Los_Angeles_Angels_of_Anaheim_season" title="2011 Los Angeles Angels of Anaheim season">Los Angeles Angels of Anaheim</a>, the Rangers acquired catcher <a href="/wiki/Mike_Napoli" title="Mike Napoli">Mike Napoli</a> in exchange for pitcher <a href="/wiki/Frank_Francisco" title="Frank Francisco">Frank Francisco</a>. During the season, the team acquired pitcher <a href="/wiki/Koji_Uehara" title="Koji Uehara">Koji Uehara</a> from the <a href="/wiki/2011_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="2011 Baltimore Orioles season">Baltimore Orioles</a> in exchange for infielder <a href="/wiki/Chris_Davis_(baseball)" title="Chris Davis (baseball)">Chris Davis</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mike_Adams_(pitcher)" title="Mike Adams (pitcher)">Mike Adams</a> from the <a href="/wiki/2011_San_Diego_Padres_season" title="2011 San Diego Padres season">San Diego Padres</a> in exchange for two minor-league pitchers. Pitcher <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Rhodes" title="Arthur Rhodes">Arthur Rhodes</a> was released and signed with the St. Louis Cardinals days later; as a result, Rhodes would have been entitled to receive a <a href="/wiki/World_Series_ring" title="World Series ring">World Series ring</a> regardless of which team won.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>With the exception of one day in late-April and a brief stretch in early-May, the Rangers led the <a href="/wiki/American_League_West" title="American League West">American League West</a> standings for most of the season. They finished the season with a franchise record 96–66 (.593 winning percentage) and won their second consecutive and fifth overall division title, 10 games ahead of the second-placers Los Angeles Angels of Anaheim. They also set a franchise for a home attendance record 2,946,949.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Texas also earned the most shutouts in the American League. All five members of the opening day starting rotation stayed in the rotation for the entire year. <a href="/wiki/C._J._Wilson" title="C. J. Wilson">C. J. Wilson</a> tied for the league lead in starts with 34 while <a href="/wiki/Derek_Holland" title="Derek Holland">Derek Holland</a> for second in shutouts with four, tied for first in the American League, and each pitcher had at least 13 wins. The offense also had another good year with three players getting 30-plus home runs for the first time in team history, and <a href="/wiki/Ian_Kinsler" title="Ian Kinsler">Ian Kinsler</a> completed his second 30–30 season.</p>
<p>The Rangers then defeated the <a href="/wiki/2011_Tampa_Bay_Rays_season" title="2011 Tampa Bay Rays season">Tampa Bay Rays</a> by three games to one in the <a href="/wiki/2011_American_League_Division_Series" title="2011 American League Division Series">American League Division Series</a> before beating the <a href="/wiki/2011_Detroit_Tigers_season" title="2011 Detroit Tigers season">Detroit Tigers</a> by four games to two in the <a href="/wiki/2011_American_League_Championship_Series" title="2011 American League Championship Series">American League Championship Series</a>.</p>
<p>The Rangers lost home-field advantage in the World Series as a result of the AL team, managed by Rangers manager <a href="/wiki/Ron_Washington" title="Ron Washington">Ron Washington</a>, losing the <a href="/wiki/2011_Major_League_Baseball_All-Star_Game" title="2011 Major League Baseball All-Star Game">2011 All-Star Game</a>, when the Ranger ace C. J. Wilson surrendered the game-winning three-run homer to <a href="/wiki/Prince_Fielder" title="Prince Fielder">Prince Fielder</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2011asg_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-2011asg-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="St._Louis_Cardinals">St. Louis Cardinals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: St. Louis Cardinals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2011_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="2011 St. Louis Cardinals season">2011 St. Louis Cardinals season</a></div>
<p>The Cardinals made their first World Series appearance since <a href="/wiki/2006_World_Series" title="2006 World Series">2006</a>, when they defeated the <a href="/wiki/2006_Detroit_Tigers_season" title="2006 Detroit Tigers season">Detroit Tigers</a> four games to one to win their National League-leading 10th World Series title. This was manager <a href="/wiki/Tony_La_Russa" title="Tony La Russa">Tony La Russa</a>'s sixth World Series appearance as manager and his third with the Cardinals. The Cardinals' last postseason appearance was in <a href="/wiki/2009_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="2009 St. Louis Cardinals season">2009</a>, where they were swept by the <a href="/wiki/2009_Los_Angeles_Dodgers_season" title="2009 Los Angeles Dodgers season">Los Angeles Dodgers</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2009_National_League_Division_Series" title="2009 National League Division Series">National League Division Series</a>. They finished the <a href="/wiki/2010_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="2010 St. Louis Cardinals season">2010 season</a> with a record of 86–76 (.531), finishing in second-place in the <a href="/wiki/National_League_Central" title="National League Central">National League Central</a> standings, five <a href="/wiki/Games_behind" title="Games behind">games behind</a> the <a href="/wiki/2010_Cincinnati_Reds_season" title="2010 Cincinnati Reds season">Cincinnati Reds</a>.</p>
<p>During the 2010 offseason, the team signed new contracts with <a href="/wiki/Manager_(baseball)" title="Manager (baseball)">manager</a> Tony La Russa and picked up all-star slugger <a href="/wiki/Albert_Pujols" title="Albert Pujols">Albert Pujols</a>' <a href="/wiki/Reserve_clause" title="Reserve clause">club option</a>. Notable offseason departures included <a href="/wiki/Shortstop" title="Shortstop">shortstop</a> <a href="/wiki/Brendan_Ryan_(baseball)" title="Brendan Ryan (baseball)">Brendan Ryan</a> (traded to the <a href="/wiki/2011_Seattle_Mariners_season" title="2011 Seattle Mariners season">Seattle Mariners</a>) and relief pitcher <a href="/wiki/Blake_Hawksworth" title="Blake Hawksworth">Blake Hawksworth</a> (traded to the <a href="/wiki/2011_Los_Angeles_Dodgers_season" title="2011 Los Angeles Dodgers season">Los Angeles Dodgers</a>). Additionally, during the offseason the team announced that <a href="/wiki/Ace_(baseball)" title="Ace (baseball)">ace</a> pitcher <a href="/wiki/Adam_Wainwright" title="Adam Wainwright">Adam Wainwright</a> would miss the entire season due to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tommy_John_surgery" title="Tommy John surgery">Tommy John surgery</a>. Notable offseason additions included shortstop <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Theriot" title="Ryan Theriot">Ryan Theriot</a>, outfielder <a href="/wiki/Lance_Berkman" title="Lance Berkman">Lance Berkman</a>, catcher <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Laird" title="Gerald Laird">Gerald Laird</a>, and infielder <a href="/wiki/Nick_Punto" title="Nick Punto">Nick Punto</a>. In late April after a number of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blown_save" title="Blown save">blown saves</a>, the Cardinals removed pitcher <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Franklin" title="Ryan Franklin">Ryan Franklin</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Closer_(baseball)" title="Closer (baseball)">closer</a> role, and released him on June 29. On July 27, the Cardinals sent outfielder <a href="/wiki/Colby_Rasmus" title="Colby Rasmus">Colby Rasmus</a> and pitchers <a href="/wiki/Trever_Miller" title="Trever Miller">Trever Miller</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brian_Tallet" title="Brian Tallet">Brian Tallet</a>, and <a href="/wiki/P._J._Walters" title="P. J. Walters">P. J. Walters</a> to the <a href="/wiki/2011_Toronto_Blue_Jays_season" title="2011 Toronto Blue Jays season">Toronto Blue Jays</a> in exchange for pitchers <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Jackson" title="Edwin Jackson">Edwin Jackson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marc_Rzepczynski" title="Marc Rzepczynski">Marc Rzepczynski</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Octavio_Dotel" title="Octavio Dotel">Octavio Dotel</a>, and outfielder <a href="/wiki/Corey_Patterson" title="Corey Patterson">Corey Patterson</a>. They then acquired <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Furcal" title="Rafael Furcal">Rafael Furcal</a> from the Dodgers in exchange for Alex Castellanos, a minor-league outfielder. On August 11, the team signed free agent pitcher <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Rhodes" title="Arthur Rhodes">Arthur Rhodes</a>, who had been released by the Texas Rangers days earlier.</p>
<p>The Cardinals spent much of the early part of the 2011 season in first-place in the NL Central standings but dropped to second-place for good on July 27. On August 25, the team trailed the <a href="/wiki/2011_Atlanta_Braves_season" title="2011 Atlanta Braves season">Atlanta Braves</a> in the NL <a href="/wiki/Wild_card_(sports)" title="Wild card (sports)">wild card</a> standings by <span class="nowrap"> </span><span class="frac nowrap">10<span class="visualhide"> </span><sup>1</sup>⁄<sub>2</sub></span> games. The Cardinals amassed a 21–9 record from August 26 to September 27, while the Braves were 10–19 over that same interval. Meanwhile, on September 23, the <a href="/wiki/2011_Milwaukee_Brewers_season" title="2011 Milwaukee Brewers season">Milwaukee Brewers</a> clinched the NL Central division title. On September 28, with the Cardinals and Braves tied atop the Wild Card standings on the last day of the regular season, the Cardinals routed the <a href="/wiki/2011_Houston_Astros_season" title="2011 Houston Astros season">Houston Astros</a> 8–0 in Houston, while the Braves lost at home to the <a href="/wiki/2011_Philadelphia_Phillies_season" title="2011 Philadelphia Phillies season">Philadelphia Phillies</a> 4–3 in 13 innings, securing the Cardinals' second wild card postseason berth in franchise history. St. Louis finished with a record of 90–72, six games behind the Brewers in the NL Central but one ahead of the Braves in the Wild Card. They defeated the Phillies in the <a href="/wiki/2011_National_League_Division_Series" title="2011 National League Division Series">National League Division Series</a> three games to two, and then defeated the Brewers in the <a href="/wiki/2011_National_League_Championship_Series" title="2011 National League Championship Series">National League Championship Series</a> four games to two.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Game_summaries">Game summaries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Game summaries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<p>Aces were on the mound for Game 1 as <a href="/wiki/C._J._Wilson" title="C. J. Wilson">C. J. Wilson</a> faced <a href="/wiki/Chris_Carpenter" title="Chris Carpenter">Chris Carpenter</a>. Both starters kept the game scoreless through the first three innings. In the fourth, <a href="/wiki/Albert_Pujols" title="Albert Pujols">Albert Pujols</a> was hit by a pitch to lead off the inning. After a double by <a href="/wiki/Matt_Holliday" title="Matt Holliday">Matt Holliday</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lance_Berkman" title="Lance Berkman">Lance Berkman</a> hit a single to drive both runners in. The lead wouldn't last long. <a href="/wiki/Mike_Napoli" title="Mike Napoli">Mike Napoli</a> hit a two-run home run to tie the game in the very next inning. <a href="/wiki/David_Freese" title="David Freese">David Freese</a> doubled in the sixth with one out, and moved to third on a wild pitch. After <a href="/wiki/Yadier_Molina" title="Yadier Molina">Yadier Molina</a> struck out, and <a href="/wiki/Nick_Punto" title="Nick Punto">Nick Punto</a> walked, <a href="/wiki/Allen_Craig" title="Allen Craig">Allen Craig</a> entered the game, pinch-hitting for Carpenter. <a href="/wiki/Alexi_Ogando" title="Alexi Ogando">Alexi Ogando</a> relieved Wilson, and tried to finish off the inning. Craig hit a 1–2 pitch down the right field line that was just out of reach of a sliding <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Cruz" title="Nelson Cruz">Nelson Cruz</a>. Freese scored to give St. Louis the lead. In the seventh, the Cardinals ran into trouble as Cruz singled and Napoli walked to put two on with one out. <a href="/wiki/Marc_Rzepczynski" title="Marc Rzepczynski">Marc Rzepczynski</a> came on to face pinch-hitter <a href="/wiki/Craig_Gentry" title="Craig Gentry">Craig Gentry</a> and struck him out. Pinch-hitter <a href="/wiki/Esteban_Germ%C3%A1n" title="Esteban Germán">Esteban Germán</a> was the next batter. Rzepczynski struck him out as well. In the ninth, closer Jason Motte pitched an easy 1–2–3 inning to give St. Louis the win. Controversy surrounded the inning, as <a href="/wiki/Adri%C3%A1n_Beltr%C3%A9" title="Adrián Beltré">Adrián Beltré</a> was the victim of a blown call. Beltré grounded a ball to third, and Descalso threw the ball to first for the out, but replays showed he fouled the ball off his foot.</p>

<td colspan="24" style="text-align:left;"><b><a href="/wiki/Win%E2%80%93loss_record_(pitching)#Winning_pitcher" title="Win–loss record (pitching)">WP</a>:</b> <a href="/wiki/Mike_Adams_(pitcher)" title="Mike Adams (pitcher)">Mike Adams</a> (1–0)   <b><a href="/wiki/Win%E2%80%93loss_record_(pitching)#Losing_pitcher" title="Win–loss record (pitching)">LP</a>:</b> <a href="/wiki/Jason_Motte" title="Jason Motte">Jason Motte</a> (0–1)   <b><a href="/wiki/Save_(baseball)" title="Save (baseball)">Sv</a>:</b> <a href="/wiki/Neftal%C3%AD_Feliz" title="Neftalí Feliz">Neftalí Feliz</a> (1)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Game 2 saw a pitchers' duel between <a href="/wiki/Jaime_Garc%C3%ADa" title="Jaime García">Jaime García</a> and <a href="/wiki/Colby_Lewis" title="Colby Lewis">Colby Lewis</a>. Both <a href="/wiki/Starting_pitcher" title="Starting pitcher">starters</a> kept the game scoreless through the first six innings. A pair of excellent defensive plays by <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Andrus" title="Elvis Andrus">Elvis Andrus</a> stopped a couple of <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals" title="St. Louis Cardinals">Cardinals</a> rallies. In the seventh, <a href="/wiki/David_Freese" title="David Freese">David Freese</a> again started a rally for St. Louis, much like in Game 1. He <a href="/wiki/Single_(baseball)" title="Single (baseball)">singled</a> with one out, and moved to third on a single by <a href="/wiki/Nick_Punto" title="Nick Punto">Nick Punto</a> with two outs. <a href="/wiki/Allen_Craig" title="Allen Craig">Allen Craig</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pinch-hit" title="Pinch-hit">pinch-hit</a> for García to face <a href="/wiki/Alexi_Ogando" title="Alexi Ogando">Alexi Ogando</a>, setting up almost the same exact situation from the previous night. Again, Craig beat Ogando with a single to right field to drive in Freese. <a href="/wiki/Jason_Motte" title="Jason Motte">Jason Motte</a> was brought in to <a href="/wiki/Save_(baseball)" title="Save (baseball)">save</a> the game in the ninth. <a href="/wiki/Ian_Kinsler" title="Ian Kinsler">Ian Kinsler</a> led off with a bloop single, and <a href="/wiki/Stolen_base" title="Stolen base">stole</a> second with Andrus batting. Andrus singled into center field, and moved to second on the throw home, which got by <a href="/wiki/Albert_Pujols" title="Albert Pujols">Albert Pujols</a> for an <a href="/wiki/Error_(baseball)" title="Error (baseball)">error</a>. With runners on second and third, and none out, <a href="/wiki/Tony_La_Russa" title="Tony La Russa">Tony La Russa</a> switched in <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Rhodes" title="Arthur Rhodes">Arthur Rhodes</a> for Motte. Consecutive <a href="/wiki/Sacrifice_fly" title="Sacrifice fly">sacrifice flies</a> from <a href="/wiki/Josh_Hamilton" title="Josh Hamilton">Josh Hamilton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michael_Young_(baseball)" title="Michael Young (baseball)">Michael Young</a> gave Texas the lead. <a href="/wiki/Neftal%C3%AD_Feliz" title="Neftalí Feliz">Neftalí Feliz</a> came on in the ninth, and allowed a leadoff <a href="/wiki/Base_on_balls" title="Base on balls">walk</a> to <a href="/wiki/Yadier_Molina" title="Yadier Molina">Yadier Molina</a>, but retired the next three batters in order to end the game and tie the <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">Series</a> at one game apiece.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Game_3">Game 3</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Game 3">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

TEX: <a href="/wiki/Michael_Young_(baseball)" title="Michael Young (baseball)">Michael Young</a> (1), <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Cruz" title="Nelson Cruz">Nelson Cruz</a> (1)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>After a total of just eight runs scored in the first two games in St. Louis, the offense of the two <a href="/wiki/Batting_order_(baseball)" title="Batting order (baseball)">lineups</a> scored a combined 23 <a href="/wiki/Run_(baseball)" title="Run (baseball)">runs</a> on a historic night in Arlington in which <a href="/wiki/Albert_Pujols" title="Albert Pujols">Albert Pujols</a> had what was described as "the greatest individual <a href="/wiki/Hit_(baseball)" title="Hit (baseball)">hitting</a> performance in World Series history".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Allen_Craig" title="Allen Craig">Allen Craig</a> hit a <a href="/wiki/Home_run" title="Home run">home run</a> in the first to put the Cardinals up 1–0. They scored four more runs in the fourth after a controversial call at first base by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Umpire" title="Umpire">umpire</a> <a href="/wiki/Ron_Kulpa" title="Ron Kulpa">Ron Kulpa</a> and a run-producing <a href="/wiki/Error_(baseball)" title="Error (baseball)">error</a> by <a href="/wiki/Mike_Napoli" title="Mike Napoli">Mike Napoli</a>, but the Rangers came back in the bottom frame: <a href="/wiki/Michael_Young_(baseball)" title="Michael Young (baseball)">Michael Young</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Cruz" title="Nelson Cruz">Nelson Cruz</a> hit home runs to make it 5–3. But in the next inning the Cardinals added three more runs including what became the game-winning two-<a href="/wiki/Run_batted_in" title="Run batted in">RBI</a> <a href="/wiki/Double_(baseball)" title="Double (baseball)">double</a> by <a href="/wiki/Yadier_Molina" title="Yadier Molina">Yadier Molina</a> making the <a href="/wiki/Score_(sport)" title="Score (sport)">score</a> 8–3. The Rangers answered with three runs in the bottom half of the inning to make it a two-run game again. <a href="/wiki/Albert_Pujols" title="Albert Pujols">Albert Pujols</a>, who had been hitless through the first two games, then hit a 423 ft (129 m) home run off <a href="/wiki/Alexi_Ogando" title="Alexi Ogando">Alexi Ogando</a> in the sixth inning to drive in three runs. He homered two more times later and drove in six runs in total on the night. The Cardinals went on to win the game by a score of 16–7, leading the Series by 2–1.</p>
<p>Albert Pujols joined <a href="/wiki/Babe_Ruth" title="Babe Ruth">Babe Ruth</a> (<a href="/wiki/1926_World_Series#Game_4" title="1926 World Series">1926</a>, <a href="/wiki/1928_World_Series#Game_4" title="1928 World Series">1928</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Reggie_Jackson" title="Reggie Jackson">Reggie Jackson</a> (<a href="/wiki/1977_World_Series#Game_6" title="1977 World Series">1977</a>) as the only players in baseball history up to that time to hit three home runs in a World Series game. (<a href="/wiki/Pablo_Sandoval" title="Pablo Sandoval">Pablo Sandoval</a> would also accomplish the feat <a href="/wiki/2012_World_Series#Game_1" title="2012 World Series">the following year</a>.) Pujols was 5-for-6 with two <a href="/wiki/Single_(baseball)" title="Single (baseball)">singles</a>, three HRs, four runs scored, and six <a href="/wiki/Run_batted_in" title="Run batted in">RBIs</a>. Yadier Molina added two doubles, driving in four runs. <a href="/wiki/David_Freese" title="David Freese">David Freese</a> continued his <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_postseason" title="Major League Baseball postseason">postseason</a> 13-game hitting streak getting two hits (one double), driving in two runs. Pujols became the first player in World Series history<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> to get hits in four <a href="/wiki/Consecutive" title="Consecutive">consecutive</a> innings: fourth (single), fifth (single), sixth (HR, three RBIs), and seventh (HR, two RBIs). He tied records for most HRs (3), most hits (5), and most RBIs (6) in a World Series game, and established a new record with 14 total bases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>The 16 runs scored by the Cardinals were the most runs scored in a World Series game since <a href="/wiki/2002_World_Series#Game_5" title="2002 World Series">2002</a>, when the <a href="/wiki/2002_San_Francisco_Giants_season" title="2002 San Francisco Giants season">San Francisco Giants</a> scored 16 against the <a href="/wiki/2002_Anaheim_Angels_season" title="2002 Anaheim Angels season">Anaheim Angels</a>. The current record is 18 by the <a href="/wiki/1936_New_York_Yankees_season" title="1936 New York Yankees season">New York Yankees</a> against the <a href="/wiki/1936_New_York_Giants_(MLB)_season" title="1936 New York Giants (MLB) season">New York Giants</a> in <a href="/wiki/1936_World_Series#Game_2" title="1936 World Series">1936</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Game_4">Game 4</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Game 4">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center;">

<p>After a high scoring affair the night before, <a href="/wiki/Derek_Holland" title="Derek Holland">Derek Holland</a> quieted the Cardinals' bats as he pitched <span class="nowrap"> </span><span class="frac nowrap">8<span class="visualhide"> </span><sup>1</sup>⁄<sub>3</sub></span> innings of two-hit baseball. <a href="/wiki/Lance_Berkman" title="Lance Berkman">Lance Berkman</a> had both of the Cardinals' two hits. <a href="/wiki/Josh_Hamilton" title="Josh Hamilton">Josh Hamilton</a>'s first-inning <a href="/wiki/Run_batted_in" title="Run batted in">RBI</a> <a href="/wiki/Double_(baseball)" title="Double (baseball)">double</a> put the Rangers in front for only the second time in the Series. A three-run home run by <a href="/wiki/Mike_Napoli" title="Mike Napoli">Mike Napoli</a> provided Holland a comfortable 4–0 lead. The Cardinals managed a small rally in the ninth, but were unable to score against closer <a href="/wiki/Neftal%C3%AD_Feliz" title="Neftalí Feliz">Neftalí Feliz</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>Coincidentally, this game was only one of two major DFW vs. St. Louis sporting events taking place in Arlington on that day, as the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">NFL</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Cowboys" title="Dallas Cowboys">Dallas Cowboys</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Louis_Rams" title="St. Louis Rams">St. Louis Rams</a> had played at nearby <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cowboys_Stadium" title="Cowboys Stadium">Cowboys Stadium</a> that afternoon; during the opening coin toss, Berkman and Hamilton, in uniform, had each served as honorary captains for their city's team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Game_5">Game 5</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Game 5">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

</tr>
</table>
<p>Game 1 <a href="/wiki/Starting_pitcher" title="Starting pitcher">starters</a> <a href="/wiki/C._J._Wilson" title="C. J. Wilson">C. J. Wilson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chris_Carpenter" title="Chris Carpenter">Chris Carpenter</a> faced off again. Wilson <a href="/wiki/Base_on_balls" title="Base on balls">walked</a> two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Batter_(baseball)" title="Batter (baseball)">batters</a>, <a href="/wiki/Matt_Holliday" title="Matt Holliday">Matt Holliday</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lance_Berkman" title="Lance Berkman">Lance Berkman</a>, in the second inning and both came in to score, aided in part by an <a href="/wiki/Error_(baseball)" title="Error (baseball)">error</a> by <a href="/wiki/David_Murphy_(baseball)" title="David Murphy (baseball)">David Murphy</a>. However, despite the Rangers walking nine batters in the game (including <a href="/wiki/Albert_Pujols" title="Albert Pujols">Albert Pujols</a> three times <a href="/wiki/Intentional_base_on_balls" title="Intentional base on balls">intentionally</a>), the Cardinals had not scored again, leaving twelve <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Left_on_base" title="Left on base">runners on base</a>. <a href="/wiki/Mitch_Moreland" title="Mitch Moreland">Mitch Moreland</a> hit a solo home run in the third, and <a href="/wiki/Adri%C3%A1n_Beltr%C3%A9" title="Adrián Beltré">Adrián Beltré</a> also hit one in the sixth, to tie the score at 2–2.</p>
<p>The Rangers' half of the eighth featured a series of <a href="/wiki/Bullpen" title="Bullpen">bullpen</a> mix-ups by the Cardinals, leaving <a href="/wiki/Tony_La_Russa" title="Tony La Russa">Tony La Russa</a> without closer <a href="/wiki/Jason_Motte" title="Jason Motte">Jason Motte</a> in a crucial situation. After <a href="/wiki/Michael_Young_(baseball)" title="Michael Young (baseball)">Michael Young</a> led off the inning with a <a href="/wiki/Double_(baseball)" title="Double (baseball)">double</a>, La Russa sent both Motte (a right-hander) and left-handed <a href="/wiki/Relief_pitcher" title="Relief pitcher">reliever</a> <a href="/wiki/Marc_Rzepczynski" title="Marc Rzepczynski">Marc Rzepczynski</a> to begin warmups. However, Cardinals bullpen coach <a href="/wiki/Derek_Lilliquist" title="Derek Lilliquist">Derek Lilliquist</a> later stated that he only heard Rzepczynski's name called. When La Russa saw that Motte was not warming up, he made a second call to the bullpen, but this time Lilliquist thought he heard La Russa called for reliever <a href="/wiki/Lance_Lynn" title="Lance Lynn">Lance Lynn</a>, who was supposedly unavailable for the game due to throwing 47 pitches in Game 3.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-g5-stl-bullpen_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-g5-stl-bullpen-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>Dotel intentionally walked <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Cruz" title="Nelson Cruz">Nelson Cruz</a>, whereupon La Russa summoned Rzepczynski to face the left-handed hitting Murphy. Usually, the Rangers would counter with a right-handed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pinch-hitter" title="Pinch-hitter">pinch-hitter</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Craig_Gentry" title="Craig Gentry">Craig Gentry</a> or <a href="/wiki/Yorvit_Torrealba" title="Yorvit Torrealba">Yorvit Torrealba</a>. However, Murphy stayed in the game, and hit a grounder off Rzepczynski, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bases_loaded" title="Bases loaded">loading the bases</a>. With Motte not yet available (La Russa thought he was warming up, but he was not yet ready), La Russa was forced to match Rzepczynski against the right-handed hitting <a href="/wiki/Mike_Napoli" title="Mike Napoli">Mike Napoli</a>, who hit a two-<a href="/wiki/Run_(baseball)" title="Run (baseball)">run</a> double scoring Young and Cruz. After a Moreland <a href="/wiki/Strikeout" title="Strikeout">strikeout</a>, La Russa summoned for Motte from the bullpen, only to be surprised to see Lynn coming out (it was then when he learned of the mix-ups). Lynn then was asked to intentionally walk <a href="/wiki/Ian_Kinsler" title="Ian Kinsler">Ian Kinsler</a>, making him only the third pitcher in World Series history to make a relief appearance solely to serve an intentional walk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-g5-stl-bullpen_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-g5-stl-bullpen-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>Neftalí Feliz came in to <a href="/wiki/Save_(baseball)" title="Save (baseball)">save</a> the game in the ninth, his second save of the Series.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Game_6">Game 6</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Game 6">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<tr style="font-size:90%;">
<td colspan="24" style="text-align:left;"><b><a href="/wiki/Win%E2%80%93loss_record_(pitching)#Winning_pitcher" title="Win–loss record (pitching)">WP</a>:</b> <a href="/wiki/Jake_Westbrook" title="Jake Westbrook">Jake Westbrook</a> (1–0)   <b><a href="/wiki/Win%E2%80%93loss_record_(pitching)#Losing_pitcher" title="Win–loss record (pitching)">LP</a>:</b> <a href="/wiki/Mark_Lowe" title="Mark Lowe">Mark Lowe</a> (0–1)<br/>
<b><a href="/wiki/Home_run" title="Home run">Home runs</a>:</b><br/>
TEX: <a href="/wiki/Adri%C3%A1n_Beltr%C3%A9" title="Adrián Beltré">Adrián Beltré</a> (2), <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Cruz" title="Nelson Cruz">Nelson Cruz</a> (2), <a href="/wiki/Josh_Hamilton" title="Josh Hamilton">Josh Hamilton</a> (1)<br/>
STL: <a href="/wiki/Lance_Berkman" title="Lance Berkman">Lance Berkman</a> (1), <a href="/wiki/Allen_Craig" title="Allen Craig">Allen Craig</a> (2), <a href="/wiki/David_Freese" title="David Freese">David Freese</a> (1)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Game 6 is considered to be one of the greatest World Series games in history. Game 6, moved from October 26 to 27 due to rain, was a rematch of Game 2's starters: Cardinals lefty <a href="/wiki/Jaime_Garc%C3%ADa" title="Jaime García">Jaime García</a> and Rangers starter <a href="/wiki/Colby_Lewis" title="Colby Lewis">Colby Lewis</a>. Texas jumped on top immediately, with <a href="/wiki/Josh_Hamilton" title="Josh Hamilton">Josh Hamilton</a> driving in <a href="/wiki/Ian_Kinsler" title="Ian Kinsler">Ian Kinsler</a> in the top of the first. The Cardinals responded quickly with a two-run <a href="/wiki/Lance_Berkman" title="Lance Berkman">Lance Berkman</a> home run in the bottom half. Kinsler tied the game in the top of the second with a ground-rule double, scoring <a href="/wiki/Craig_Gentry" title="Craig Gentry">Craig Gentry</a>. García was pulled after only three innings (and 59 pitches) and replaced with <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Salas" title="Fernando Salas">Fernando Salas</a>. Leading off the top of the fourth, <a href="/wiki/Matt_Holliday" title="Matt Holliday">Matt Holliday</a> misplayed a <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Cruz" title="Nelson Cruz">Nelson Cruz</a> pop fly, putting Cruz at second. <a href="/wiki/Mike_Napoli" title="Mike Napoli">Mike Napoli</a> singled him home to once again give Texas the lead.</p>
<p>The Cardinals jumped right back in the game, taking advantage of a <a href="/wiki/Michael_Young_(baseball)" title="Michael Young (baseball)">Michael Young</a> error and scoring on a <a href="/wiki/Yadier_Molina" title="Yadier Molina">Yadier Molina</a> groundout to knot the game at three. <a href="/wiki/David_Freese" title="David Freese">David Freese</a> started off the top of the fifth by dropping a routine pop fly (the third consecutive half-inning to begin with an error), which immediately turned into the go-ahead run for Texas on Young's double. Colby Lewis was cruising for the Rangers until the bottom of the sixth. After an <a href="/wiki/Albert_Pujols" title="Albert Pujols">Albert Pujols</a> strikeout, Berkman singled to third. Matt Holliday grounded into a possible double play which was mishandled at first by Michael Young (his second error of the game), leaving all runners safe. Lewis walked the bases loaded and was pulled for <a href="/wiki/Alexi_Ogando" title="Alexi Ogando">Alexi Ogando</a>, who promptly walked Yadier Molina to force in a run. With the Cardinals in a prime position to rally ahead, Matt Holliday, standing 90 feet (27 m) away as the possible go-ahead run, was picked off at third by catcher Mike Napoli. Holliday injured his finger sliding in on the play and was forced to leave the game. The Rangers were able to slip out of the inning with the score still tied.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Lance_Lynn" title="Lance Lynn">Lance Lynn</a> came on to pitch for the Cardinals in the top of the seventh and was promptly greeted with back-to-back home runs by <a href="/wiki/Adri%C3%A1n_Beltr%C3%A9" title="Adrián Beltré">Adrián Beltré</a> and Nelson Cruz to put Texas up by two. Ian Kinsler added his second RBI later in the inning to make the score 7–4 Rangers. In the bottom of the eighth, <a href="/wiki/Allen_Craig" title="Allen Craig">Allen Craig</a> (who entered the game as Holliday's replacement) hit a solo home run to pull the Cardinals within two. Rangers closer <a href="/wiki/Neftal%C3%AD_Feliz" title="Neftalí Feliz">Neftalí Feliz</a> entered in the bottom of the ninth to deliver the Rangers their first ever World Series Championship. After striking out <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Theriot" title="Ryan Theriot">Ryan Theriot</a>, Feliz faced Albert Pujols. Facing possibly his last at-bat as a Cardinal, Pujols hit Feliz's first pitch into left field for a double. Feliz walked Lance Berkman to put the tying run on first, but got Craig to take a called third strike. The Rangers were one out away from a championship as David Freese stepped to the plate. Down in the count 1–2 and down to the last strike, Freese hit Feliz's pitch past a leaping Nelson Cruz off the wall for a triple, tying the game at seven in dramatic fashion.</p>
<p>Sent into extra innings, Jason Motte went out for his second inning of work. Elvis Andrus singled, then the Rangers' MVP candidate Josh Hamilton put Texas up again with a towering two-run home run. Down 9–7, and out of bench players, the Cardinals once again faced only three outs until elimination. Left-hander Darren Oliver came in to pitch for the Rangers. St. Louis Players <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Descalso" title="Daniel Descalso">Daniel Descalso</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jon_Jay" title="Jon Jay">Jon Jay</a> got back-to-back singles, and starting pitcher <a href="/wiki/Kyle_Lohse" title="Kyle Lohse">Kyle Lohse</a> was called to bunt. Lohse's sacrifice bunt put the tying run in scoring position. With right-handers coming up, right-hander <a href="/wiki/Scott_Feldman" title="Scott Feldman">Scott Feldman</a> replaced Oliver on the mound. <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Theriot" title="Ryan Theriot">Ryan Theriot</a> grounded out, scoring Descalso, and following an intentional walk to Pujols, Berkman stepped up to the plate. Feldmen got ahead on the count 1-2. Berkman worked the count to 2–2, and again the Rangers were one strike away from their first championship. Berkman took <a href="/wiki/Scott_Feldman" title="Scott Feldman">Scott Feldman</a>'s next pitch into center field for a single, scoring <a href="/wiki/Jon_Jay" title="Jon Jay">Jon Jay</a> and tying the game once again. It was the first time in World Series history that a team came back from two different two-run deficits in the ninth inning or later in the same game.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The Rangers failed to score in the top of the 11th, bringing David Freese to lead off the bottom of the inning. Freese hit <a href="/wiki/Mark_Lowe" title="Mark Lowe">Mark Lowe</a>'s 3–2 pitch into the center field grass for a game-winning home run, forcing the World Series to a Game 7 for the first time since <a href="/wiki/2002_World_Series" title="2002 World Series">2002</a>.</p>
<p>Of the last 13 instances in which a Major League team won a Game 6 at home to force a Game 7 in the postseason, all but two went on to win Game 7. The exceptions were the <a href="/wiki/2006_New_York_Mets_season" title="2006 New York Mets season">New York Mets</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2006_NLCS" title="2006 NLCS">2006 NLCS</a> against, coincidentally, the <a href="/wiki/2006_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="2006 St. Louis Cardinals season">Cardinals</a>; and the Boston Red Sox in the 1975 World Series against the Cincinnati Reds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Game_6_win_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-Game_6_win-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>Freese's walk-off home run was the fourth that won<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> in a Game 6 in World Series history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Cardinals set two World Series milestones in their Game 6 win—the first team to come back from deficits in both the 9th and 10th innings, and the first team to score in the 8th, 9th, 10th, and 11th innings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> On <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mike_and_Mike_in_the_Morning" title="Mike and Mike in the Morning">Mike and Mike in the Morning</a></i> the next day, <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a> senior baseball analyst <a href="/wiki/Buster_Olney" title="Buster Olney">Buster Olney</a> called it the greatest game in the history of baseball.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>Game 6 was originally scheduled for Wednesday, October 26, but was postponed due to heavy rain in the forecast. Although rain was only falling fairly lightly in St. Louis when this decision was made, MLB officials did not want a repeat of <a href="/wiki/2008_World_Series#Game_5" title="2008 World Series">Game 5 of the 2008 World Series</a>, which was suspended after the top of the sixth inning and resumed two days later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Game_6_ppd_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-Game_6_ppd-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>David Freese and Lance Berkman became the third and fourth players<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> in World Series history to get game-tying hits with their team one out from elimination.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schoen_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-schoen-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>Freese, who grew up a Cardinal fan in the suburbs of St. Louis, said that as he was circling the bases after his home run, he was thinking about a similar walk-off homer by <a href="/wiki/Jim_Edmonds" title="Jim Edmonds">Jim Edmonds</a> for the <a href="/wiki/2004_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="2004 St. Louis Cardinals season">Cardinals</a> in <a href="/wiki/2004_National_League_Championship_Series#Game_6" title="2004 National League Championship Series">Game 6 of the 2004 National League Championship Series</a>. After Freese said he remembered that home run, Lance Berkman, who played for the losing <a href="/wiki/2004_Houston_Astros_season" title="2004 Houston Astros season">Houston Astros</a> in that series, said "So do I."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Game_7">Game 7</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Game 7">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p>Before Game 7, the Cardinals replaced <a href="/wiki/Matt_Holliday" title="Matt Holliday">Matt Holliday</a>, who sprained his wrist in Game 6, on their roster with <a href="/wiki/Adron_Chambers" title="Adron Chambers">Adron Chambers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>Josh Hamilton and Michael Young had RBI doubles in the first inning against Chris Carpenter, who became the first pitcher in a decade<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> to make three starts in one Series. David Freese had a game-tying two-run double in the bottom of the first, breaking the post-season RBI record, and Allen Craig hit a go-ahead homer in the third. Craig even robbed a home run from <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Cruz" title="Nelson Cruz">Nelson Cruz</a> in the sixth. St. Louis added two runs off Scott Feldman in the fifth inning without getting a hit. Yadier Molina walked with the bases loaded, C. J. Wilson came on to relieve Feldman and promptly hit Rafael Furcal with his first pitch, forcing in another run to make it 5–2.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> In the seventh inning, Lance Berkman scored on a Molina single to make it 6–2.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>Chris Carpenter was relieved after pitching six innings and was credited with the win. The Cardinals used four <a href="/wiki/Relief_pitcher" title="Relief pitcher">relievers</a> to hold Texas scoreless over the final three innings. The final out was recorded when Jason Motte got <a href="/wiki/David_Murphy_(baseball)" title="David Murphy (baseball)">David Murphy</a> to fly out to Cardinal left fielder <a href="/wiki/Allen_Craig" title="Allen Craig">Allen Craig</a> as Busch Stadium went into a frenzy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/David_Freese" title="David Freese">David Freese</a> became the sixth player in history to earn a <a href="/wiki/League_Championship_Series_Most_Valuable_Player_Award" title="League Championship Series Most Valuable Player Award">League Championship Series</a> and <a href="/wiki/World_Series_Most_Valuable_Player_Award" title="World Series Most Valuable Player Award">World Series MVP award</a> in the same postseason.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Rangers set a Series record by issuing 41 walks, breaking the previous record held by the <a href="/wiki/1997_Florida_Marlins_season" title="1997 Florida Marlins season">Florida Marlins</a> when winning the <a href="/wiki/1997_World_Series" title="1997 World Series">1997 World Series</a> after issuing 40.</p>
<p>The Cardinals became the first wild card team to win the World Series since the <a href="/wiki/2004_Boston_Red_Sox_season" title="2004 Boston Red Sox season">Boston Red Sox</a> won the <a href="/wiki/2004_World_Series" title="2004 World Series">2004 World Series</a> (coincidentally, against the Cardinals).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Composite_box">Composite box</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Composite box">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>2011 World Series <b>(4–3): <a href="/wiki/2011_St._Louis_Cardinals_season" title="2011 St. Louis Cardinals season">St. Louis Cardinals</a> (N.L.)</b> over <a href="/wiki/2011_Texas_Rangers_season" title="2011 Texas Rangers season">Texas Rangers</a> (A.L.)</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Broadcasting">Broadcasting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Broadcasting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Television">Television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The series was televised in the United States and Canada by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_on_Fox#Postseason_coverage" title="Major League Baseball on Fox">Fox</a>. <a href="/wiki/Joe_Buck" title="Joe Buck">Joe Buck</a> called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Play-by-play" title="Play-by-play">play-by-play</a> on his 14th World Series for the network, dating back to <a href="/wiki/1996_World_Series" title="1996 World Series">1996</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Color_commentator" title="Color commentator">color analyst</a> <a href="/wiki/Tim_McCarver" title="Tim McCarver">Tim McCarver</a> handled his 22nd World Series since <a href="/wiki/1985_World_Series" title="1985 World Series">1985</a>. <a href="/wiki/Ken_Rosenthal" title="Ken Rosenthal">Ken Rosenthal</a> served as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Field_reporter" title="Field reporter">field reporter</a> for the games, while <a href="/wiki/Chris_Rose" title="Chris Rose">Chris Rose</a> hosted the pregame and postgame coverage with analysts <a href="/wiki/A._J._Pierzynski" title="A. J. Pierzynski">A. J. Pierzynski</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eric_Karros" title="Eric Karros">Eric Karros</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>Joe Buck's call of ... we will see you tomorrow night!" on David Freese's walk-off home run echoed his father Jack's call from Game 6 of the 1991 World Series, occurring 20 years and a day apart from each other, given the similar situations: Game 6, first batter of the final inning, and breaking a 3-3 tie to win the game 4-3, and extend the series to a 7th game.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/MLB_International" title="MLB International">MLB International</a> syndicated television coverage of the Series (with <a href="/wiki/Gary_Thorne" title="Gary Thorne">Gary Thorne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rick_Sutcliffe" title="Rick Sutcliffe">Rick Sutcliffe</a> announcing) to viewers outside of North America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ratings">Ratings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Ratings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The ratings started off poorly, averaging just 8.4 through its first 5 games (at this time, the record for lowest World Series rating was 8.4, set by the 5 games 2008 World Series and the 5 games 2010 World Series). Game 3 also produced a 6.6 rating, making it the second lowest World Series rated game of all-time (behind the 6.1 rating in Game 3 of the 2008 World Series and Game 3 of the 2012 World Series).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>However, Games 6 and 7 generated massive ratings that brought the overall average to 9.9. The 14.7 rating for Game 7 is the network's highest for a World Series telecast since <a href="/wiki/2004_World_Series#Game_4" title="2004 World Series">Game 4 of the 2004 World Series</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio">Radio</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Radio">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_on_ESPN_Radio" title="Major League Baseball on ESPN Radio">ESPN Radio</a> also broadcast the games nationally. This was the first World Series for play-by play announcer <a href="/wiki/Dan_Shulman" title="Dan Shulman">Dan Shulman</a> and analysts <a href="/wiki/Orel_Hershiser" title="Orel Hershiser">Orel Hershiser</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Valentine" title="Bobby Valentine">Bobby Valentine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fang_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fang-49">[49]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/ESPN_Deportes_Radio" title="ESPN Deportes Radio">ESPN Deportes Radio</a> aired the Series for <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish language</a> listeners, with Ernesto Jerez and Guillermo Celis announcing.</p>
<p>Locally, the two teams' <a href="/wiki/Flagship_(broadcasting)" title="Flagship (broadcasting)">flagship stations</a> broadcast the Series with their respective announcing crews. The Rangers' broadcasts aired on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/KESN-FM" title="KESN-FM">KESN-FM</a> (with <a href="/wiki/Eric_Nadel" title="Eric Nadel">Eric Nadel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Steve_Busby" title="Steve Busby">Steve Busby</a> announcing),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> while the Cardinals' broadcasts aired on <a href="/wiki/KMOX" title="KMOX">KMOX</a> (with <a href="/wiki/Mike_Shannon" title="Mike Shannon">Mike Shannon</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Rooney_(sportscaster)" title="John Rooney (sportscaster)">John Rooney</a> announcing).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> Due to contractual obligations, the non-flagship stations on the teams' radio networks carried the ESPN Radio broadcasts of the games, although the local broadcasts were available on <a href="/wiki/XM_Satellite_Radio" title="XM Satellite Radio">XM Satellite Radio</a> and to Gameday Audio subscribers at <a href="/wiki/MLB.com" title="MLB.com">MLB.com</a>.</p>
<p>In the United Kingdom, <a href="/wiki/Simon_Brotherton" title="Simon Brotherton">Simon Brotherton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Josh_Chetwynd" title="Josh Chetwynd">Josh Chetwynd</a> called the games for <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_5_Live_Sports_Extra" title="BBC Radio 5 Live Sports Extra">BBC Radio 5 Live Sports Extra</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Aftermath">Aftermath</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_World_Series&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Aftermath">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TonyLarussa1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1728" data-file-width="2592" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/TonyLarussa1.jpg/220px-TonyLarussa1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/TonyLarussa1.jpg/330px-TonyLarussa1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/TonyLarussa1.jpg/440px-TonyLarussa1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:TonyLarussa1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
La Russa during the World Series parade.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The 2011 World Series was only the second World Series ever in which a team, one strike away from elimination, came back to win—with the Cardinals, in fact, achieving this feat twice in Game 6. The first was the <a href="/wiki/1986_World_Series" title="1986 World Series">1986 World Series</a>, in which the New York Mets rallied from a 5–3 deficit in the bottom of the 10th inning of Game 6 to win the game and, later, the decisive Game 7.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>This was the third and final World Series title for Cardinals manager <a href="/wiki/Tony_La_Russa" title="Tony La Russa">Tony La Russa</a>, who announced his retirement on October 31, 2011, after 33 seasons as a major league manager.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LaRussaretires_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-LaRussaretires-55">[55]</a></sup> La Russa had previously led the Cardinals (<a href="/wiki/2006_World_Series" title="2006 World Series">2006</a>) and <a href="/wiki/1989_Oakland_Athletics_season" title="1989 Oakland Athletics season">Oakland Athletics</a> (<a href="/wiki/1989_World_Series" title="1989 World Series">1989</a>) to World Series championships. Former Cardinals catcher <a href="/wiki/Mike_Matheny" title="Mike Matheny">Mike Matheny</a>, who played for the <a href="/wiki/2004_World_Series" title="2004 World Series">2004</a> Cardinals that lost the World Series, was hired to replace him.</p>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Giants" title="New York Giants">New York Giants</a> won <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XLVI" title="Super Bowl XLVI">Super Bowl XLVI</a> during the offseason, some news organizations, among them <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_St._Louis_Post-Dispatch" title="The St. Louis Post-Dispatch">The St. Louis Post-Dispatch</a></i>, compared the Cardinals to the Giants, invoking <a href="/wiki/Al_Michaels" title="Al Michaels">Al Michaels</a>'s call of the Giants winning the Super Bowl: "The New York Giants, given the last rites by many in December, are the Super Bowl Champs in February."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Rangers became the first team to lose in the World Series in consecutive years since the <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Braves" title="Atlanta Braves">Atlanta Braves</a> in <a href="/wiki/1991_World_Series" title="1991 World Series">1991</a> and <a href="/wiki/1992_World_Series" title="1992 World Series">1992</a> and the first American League team to do so since the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a> in <a href="/wiki/1963_World_Series" title="1963 World Series">1963</a> and <a href="/wiki/1964_World_Series" title="1964 World Series">1964</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Albert_Pujols" title="Albert Pujols">Albert Pujols</a> and <a href="/wiki/C._J._Wilson" title="C. J. Wilson">C. J. Wilson</a> would later end up signing with the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Angels_of_Anaheim" title="Los Angeles Angels of Anaheim">Los Angeles Angels of Anaheim</a> in the offseason, in one of the deepest free-agent classes in recent MLB history, while the Rangers obtained the <a href="/wiki/Posting_system" title="Posting system">rights</a> to sign Japanese star pitcher <a href="/wiki/Yu_Darvish" title="Yu Darvish">Yu Darvish</a> to replace Wilson. In his first press conference as a Ranger, Darvish was asked about Game 6 of the World Series where <a href="/wiki/David_Freese" title="David Freese">David Freese</a> hit walk-off home run in the bottom of the 11th, and said "If it was last year [2011], I would have given up a home run and lost the game. This year [2012] I won't let that happen."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>Both teams would advance again into the postseason in the following year, both as wild cards entrants. The Rangers lost to the <a href="/wiki/2012_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="2012 Baltimore Orioles season">Baltimore Orioles</a> in the inaugural <a href="/wiki/2012_American_League_Wild_Card_Game" title="2012 American League Wild Card Game">American League Wild Card game</a>, and would not make the post season again until 2015. The Cardinals won the inaugural <a href="/wiki/2012_National_League_Wild_Card_Game" title="2012 National League Wild Card Game">National League Wild Card game</a> against Atlanta before displaying more comeback magic in defeating the <a href="/wiki/2012_Washington_Nationals_season" title="2012 Washington Nationals season">Washington Nationals</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2012_National_League_Division_Series" title="2012 National League Division Series">NLDS</a> in five games. After having a 3–1 series lead against the <a href="/wiki/2012_San_Francisco_Giants_season" title="2012 San Francisco Giants season">San Francisco Giants</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2012_National_League_Championship_Series" title="2012 National League Championship Series">NLCS</a>, the Cardinals fell one game short of a return trip to the World Series in losing each of the final three games to end the season.</p>
<p>St. Louis would return to the World Series in <a href="/wiki/2013_World_Series" title="2013 World Series">2013</a>, continuing the pattern of Giants and Cardinals exchanging pennant victories. However, the Cardinals lost to the <a href="/wiki/2013_Boston_Red_Sox_season" title="2013 Boston Red Sox season">Boston Red Sox</a> in six games despite leading 2–1.</p>
<p>La Russa would be inducted into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Baseball_Hall_of_Fame" title="National Baseball Hall of Fame">National Baseball Hall of Fame</a> in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LaRussaHOF_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-LaRussaHOF-58">[58]</a></sup></p>

<td colspan="2"></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="3">
<div>No World Series was held in <a href="/wiki/1904_World_Series" title="1904 World Series">1904</a> because the <a href="/wiki/1904_New_York_Giants_season" title="1904 New York Giants season">NL champions</a> refused to participate; no World Series was held in <a href="/wiki/1994_World_Series" title="1994 World Series">1994</a> due to <a href="/wiki/1994%E2%80%9395_Major_League_Baseball_strike" title="1994–95 Major League Baseball strike">a players' strike</a>.</div>
</td>
</tr>
